тАШрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдВ рддреЗ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╛рдЧрд╕реНрддреНрд╕реНрдпрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ред рдЖрджреНрдпреИрдиреНрджреНрд░реА рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдорд░реБрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рд╣рд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН ред тАШрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд╛рджреНрдпреИрдиреНрджреНрд░реА’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

167
Maruts (except Indra 1)
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
A particularly fine example of AgastyaтАЩs poetic skill. The first few verses invite first Indra (vs. 1) and then the Maruts (vs. 2) to come to us; the last few verses (8тАУ10) before the refrain (vs. 11) celebrate the massive strength of the Maruts (vss. 8cdтАУ9), and again express the hope that Indra and the Maruts will stand by us (vs. 10), with a curious detour through the topic of the ─АdityasтАЩ protective powers (vs. 8ab).
But the heart of the hymn (vss. 3тАУ7) is devoted to the MarutsтАЩ relationship with their consort Rodas─л, whose name is identical, save for accent, with the dual referring to the тАЬtwo world-halvesтАЭ (rodas─л versus ╠Б ro╠Бdas─л, though the latter can also some times be used for Rodas─л). The verses are marked by what in Classical Sanskrit poetry would be called ┼Ыleс╣гa (тАЬpunningтАЭ), and the tone is curiously mixed: Rodas─л is both extravagantly praised and at the same time scornfully compared to a loose woman, with those two incompatible attitudes conveyed in the same words. (Unfortunately, the understated deftness of these verbal plays is overwhelmed by our necessarily labored and clumsy explanations.) For example, in verse 3 Rodas─л is compared to a young woman running after men by going to the public gaming hall, but also com
pared to fine ceremonial speech appropriate to a public occasion. The same word (sabh─Б╠Бvat─л) is used both for her shameful appearance in the public hall and her role as speech honored in public. In verse 4 the word s─Бdh─Бraс╣Зy─Б╠Б тАЬcommonтАЭ is used both of the MarutsтАЩ joint cherishing of Rodas─л and in a simile comparing her to a whore. (This kind of verbal condemnation of a polyandrous woman is familiar in later Sanskrit in the taunts sometimes directed to the noble Draupad─л, wife of the five P─Бс╣Зс╕Нavas in the Mah─Бbh─Бrata.) A complex pun in the second half of verse 4 plays with the partial identity of Rodas─л and the two world-halves; the grammatical aspects of this pun cannot be treated here. Despite the somewhat slighting treatment in the similes of verses 3тАУ4, Rodas─л takes on the role of bride in verses 5тАУ6 by mounting the nuptial chariot like the mythological model of the bride, S┼лry─Б. This depiction of ceremonial marriage provides a transition to the ritual here-and-now (vss. 6cdтАУ7), where not only the Maruts, but also Rodas─л along with the Wives of the Gods, appear at our ritual.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your thousand benefits, Indra, come to us; may a thousand kinds of abundant food come to us, lord of horses; may a thousand (sorts of wealth) come to exhilarate us; may thousands of horses be ours.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

A thousand are your forms of help to us, o Indra, a thousand your most welcomed refreshments, o possessor of the fallow bays,
a thousand your riches, to exhilarate us. Let your thousandfold prizes come near to us.

Griffith

A THOUSAND are thy helps for us, O Indra: a thousand, Lord of Bays, thy choice refreshments.
Wealth of a thousand sorts hast thou to cheer us: may precious goods come nigh to us in thousands.

Geldner

Du hast, o Indra, tausend Hilfen f├╝r uns, tausend sehr willkommene Labsale, du Falbenlenker. Tausend Reicht├╝mer, tausendf├дltige Gewinne sollen uns zukommen, um uns zu erfreuen!

Grassmann

Zu tausenden sind Indra deine H├╝lfen und sehr willkommnen Labungen, o Rossherr, Zu tausenden die Gaben uns zur Freude, und tausend Kr├дfte m├╢gen in uns eingehn.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the Maruts come to our presence with benefaction; may they who are possessed of knowledge (come) with most excellent and brilliant (treasures), since their glorious horses, the Niyutas, gather wealth even on the farther shore of the sea.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Samudrasya cid dhanayanta p─Бra, bearing or collecting wealth, even on the farther shore of the sea; parasmin, on the other bank; metaphorically, the explanation is: winds bring wealth, i.e. rain, from the skirts of the horizon or firmament

Jamison Brereton

Let the Maruts, masters of artifice, drive hither to us with their help, or with their preeminent, heaven-lofty (riches?),
even when they, while furthest away, are running their teams on the far shore of the seaтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

┼Ыubh├й k├бm y─Бnti тАж). However, the juxtaposition of the first two words in III.26.4 ┼Ыubh├й s├бmmi┼Ыl─Бс╕е pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гat─лr ayukс╣гata is suggestive of a connection here between ┼Ыubh├й and n├нmi┼Ыl─Бm (though in the published translation of III.26.4 ┼Ыubh├й is not construed with s├бmmi┼Ыl─Бс╕е but with ayukс╣гata). Still I remain inclined towards my тАЬmount for beauty,тАЭ because I think n├нmi┼Ыl─Бm refers to Rodas─лтАЩs intimate connection with the Maruts, which was emphasized at the very beginning of the mythological section, 3a mimy├бkс╣гa y├йс╣гu тАж, hence my тАЬcommingling (with them).тАЭ As was just noted, I take 6ab as the end of the little Rodas─л myth and 6cd as the beginning of the section treating the current ritual. I therefore (contra the standard tr.) take cd as dependent on 7, not on 6ab.

Griffith

May the most sapient Maruts, with protection, with best boons brought from lofty heaven, approach us,
Now when their team of the most noble horses speeds even on the sea’s extremest limit.

Geldner

Die Marut sollen mit ihren Hilfen zu uns kommen oder mit den h├╢chsten, vom Himmel stammenden, die Verwandlungsk├╝nstler, auch wenn ihre entferntesten Gespanne noch am anderen Ufer des Meeres laufen.

Grassmann

Mit H├╝lfen m├╢gen uns die Maruts nahen, mit himmlischen, vorz├╝glichsten, die weisen; Selbst dann, wenn ihre herrlichen Gespanne auch an des Meeres fernstem Ufer laufen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn whom the water-shedding, golden-coloured lighting, is fitly deposited like a chaplet (of clouds) moving in the firmament like the (splendidly-attired) wife of a man (of rank), and distinguished in assemblies like a sacrificial hymn.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Guh─Б caranti manuс╣гo na yoс╣г─Б, going in the darkness of the sky, as if it was in private or in secret, like the wife of a man, who, although, is brilliantly attired, remains in the privacy of the feminine le apartments, suveс╣г─Бntahpura eva madhye carati; distinguished in assemblies: sabh─Бvati vidatheva sam. v─Бk; the first is referred to the lightning, which, at times, shows itself as if in an assembly, sabh─Б; the reference may also be to yoс╣г─Б, a woman who is not always restricted to the private chambers, but appears occasionally in public

Jamison Brereton

(The Maruts), to whom (Rodas─л) has been joined, positioned well, up close to them like their own spearтАФshe ghee-rich, garbed in gold,
roving in secret, like a young woman going to men when sheтАЩs bound for the public hall [/provided with a public forum] like ceremonial speech.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the punning and diametrically opposed, negative and positive readings of this vs. mediated by sabh─Б╠Бvat─л, see the published introduction. Rodas─л is depiced both as fit for the sabh─Б (gaming hall) like a young woman who goes there in secret [=whore], but also fit for the sabh─Б (assembly) like speech to be publicly uttered there (cf. the sabh├йyo v├нpraс╕е тАЬthe inspired poet appropriate to the sabh─Б in II.24.13). For the association between the sabh─Б and licentious sexual activity, see Falk (Bruderschaft, 90-92).

Geldner (/Hoffmann, Witzel Got┼Н) take ├║par─Б тАж с╣Ыс╣гс╣н├нс╕е as the lower part of the spear and consider the shared characteristic between simile and frame to be h├нraс╣Зyanirс╣Зik тАШgarbed in goldтАЩ, presumably referring to the decorated hilt or handle of the spear.

But I take ├║par─Б as meaning тАШnearer, very closeтАЩ (so approx. Renou) and the point of comparison is how close Rodas─л is to the Maruts (тАЬto whom she has been joined, positioned wellтАЭ: mimy├бkс╣гa y├йс╣гu s├║dhit─Б) – as close as their spear, which is attached to their shoulders: cf. I.64.4 ├бс╣Гseс╣гv eс╣г─Бс╣Г n├н mimс╣Ыkс╣гur с╣Ыс╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е тАЬOn their shoulders spears have rubbed.тАЭ (The verbs mimy├бkс╣гa and mimс╣Ыkс╣гuс╕е belong to different roots, but echo each other phonetically.) The standard tr. take m├бnuс╣гaс╕е as gen. sg., dependent on y├│с╣г─Б, whereas I see it as acc. pl. Either is of course grammatically possible.

Hoffmann (194-95, fld. by Witzel Got┼Н) sees s├бс╣Г v─Б╠Бk as a new, separate clause (тАЬDabei ist die V─Бc.тАЭ). Although I donтАЩt entirely understand the position and function of s├бm, I do not think making these last two words into an abrupt appendage works well.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe radiant, ever-moving Maruts, have mingled with (their) associate, (lightning), like (youths) with common women; the formidable divinities do not overwhelm heaven and earth (with rain), but promote their prosperity through (friendly) regard.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With a common woman: s─Бdh─Бraс╣Зyeva = a public, or common woman

Jamison Brereton

Away (went) the resplendent, irrepressible Maruts in their flood; they joined (with her) in common, as if with a common (whore).
The fearsome ones did not push Rodas─л away as they did push the two world-halves apart. The gods took pleasure in strengthening (her/
them), for companionship.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The polarized positive/negative treatment of Rodas─л continues in the first half of this vs., in my interpr. With Hoffmann (/Witzel Got┼Н) I take p─Бda a as separate from b and supply a verb of motion with p├бr─Б тАШawayтАЩ. In b, in my interpr. only, the fem.

instr. s─Бdh─Бraс╣Зy─Б╠БтАШcommonтАЩ refers both to the fact that Rodas─л is held by them in common and that this type of relationship leaves her open to the charge that she is no better than a whore. (As noted in the published introduction, even Draupad─л in the Mah─Бbh─Бrata sometimes receives this insult because she is the common wife of all the P─Бс╣Зс╕Нavas.) The 2nd hemistich puns on the name Rodas─л (once again, this is only my interpr; others see it very differently), providing us with a grammatical problem. The form found in the text, rodas─л╠Б, should by accent be the name of the MarutsтАЩ consort, but as a singular -─л-stem, it should be nominative, a grammatical identity that does not fit the context well. Oldenberg takes it as an instr. Geldner suggests that the word here is flexionslos, which conveniently allows him to construe it as an acc. with ├бpa nudanta (so also Renou, without comment on the morphology). Hoffmann (fld. by Witzel Got┼Н) suggests itтАЩs an elliptical dual, standing for Rodas─л and V─Бc. I instead think it is a grammatical compromise that enables a pun – a compromise between dual *r├│das─л, the standard word for the two world halves (so accented) and sg. *rodas─л╠Бm, the acc. sg. of the personal name. In other words, the rodas─л╠Бwe have in the text is a formal compromise: the right form for the dual worlds but the wrong accent; the right accent for the singular woman but the wrong case form. This is where the pun comes in, depending on a further implied pun on the n├б that opens the line. On the one hand it is the negative, to be read with the personal name: тАЬdid not push Rodas─л awayтАЭ (so most tr.); on the other hand it is the simile marker, to be read with the two worlds: тАЬas they did push apart the two world halves.тАЭ This refers to the cosmogonic deed, generally attributed to Indra, of separating the two world halves to create living space between them. The n├б is of course in the wrong position for the simile marker, but I think Agastya relies on his audience to actualize his plays on words with hints like this. The full version of this very condensed expression would be n├б *rodas─л╠Б(m) [/r├│das─л] n├б тАЬnot Rodas─л like the two world halves.

In the next p─Бda both Rodas─л and the two world halves are then the objects of a (quasi-)infinitival vс╣Ы╠Бdham (again, my interpr. differs from othersтАЩ). Cf. the similar expression in I.85.1c r├│das─л h├н mar├║ta┼Ы cakrir├й vr╠еdh├й тАЬthe Maruts made the two world halves grow strong,тАЭ with a clear dative infinitive in periphrastic causative usage. The only other ex. of acc. vс╣Ы╠Бdham in III.16.2 also has infinitival value and even has the Maruts as subj.

Hoffmann (Injunk., 194-97) translates and comments on these verses.

Griffith

Far off the brilliant, never-weary Maruts cling to the young Maid as a joint possession.
The fierce Gods drave not Rodasi before them, but wished for her to grow their friend and fellow.

Die schmucken, unverzagten Marut zogen mit der Unparteilichen wie mit einer gemeinsamen Frau davon. Die Grausigen stie├Яen die Rodasi nicht ab, die G├╢tter lie├Яen sich die Starke zur Gesellschaft gerne gefallen.

Grassmann

Das fernste auch besprengten sie, die lichten behenden Maruts wie mit gleichem Strome; Gemeinsam m├╢gen sie den Krafttrunk nehmen, die Schreckensg├╢tter nicht die Braut verscheuchen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRodas─л, the associate of the scatterers (of the clouds), with dishevelled tresses, and mind devoted to her lords, woos them to associate (with her); radiant in form, she has ascended the car of the restless (Maruts) as S┼лrya (ascended the car of the A┼Ыvins), and comes hither (with the celerity) of the sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rodas─л = heaven and earth; here, it signifies the lightning; or the bride of the Maruts, marutpatn─л vidyud v─Б;

S┼лrya: s┼лryeva, like s┼лrya; either the wife or the daughter of s┼лrya

Jamison Brereton

If it please her ladyship to accompany themтАФRodas─л with unloosened braid had her mind set on the menтАФ
like S┼лry─Б she mounts the chariot of the one who does honor, she whose face is turbulent like the approach of a cloud.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. depicts a svayaс╣Гvara (self-choice) marriage likened to the mythological prototype of the svayaс╣Гvara, that of S┼лry─Б. The identification of the two female figures is underlined by the echo between asur├н y─Б тАШher ladyshipтАЩ (p─Бda, referring to Rodas─л) and ─Б╠Бs┼лr i y─Б (opening p─Бda c, naming S┼лry─Б).

j├│с╣гat is an aor. subjunctive. As the first word of the verse, it introduces the тАЬchoiceтАЭ theme. I take j├│с╣гad y├бd as a type of politeness formula тАЬif X will be pleased to тАж,тАЭ archaic English тАЬan it please тАжтАЭ Note that dat. sac├бdhyai тАШto accompanyтАЩ is complementary to dat. sakhy─Б╠Бya тАШfor companionshipтАЩ in 4d and of course etymologically related. The complementarity extends to the implied subjects: in 4d the Maruts are taking steps to produce companionship; in 5a it is Rodas─л who decides to accompany them.

The bahuvr─лhi nс╣Ыm├бс╣Зas- usually means тАШmanly mindedтАЩ and so it is interpr.

here by most (Geldner [/Hoffmann/Witzel Got┼Н] тАШmannhaftgesinntтАЩ; Renou тАШlтАЩ├вme virileтАЩ). But though she does display a fair amount of gumption, I find this an odd characterization of the very feminine Rodas─л. In this context I take it rather as тАШhaving her mind on (the) menтАЩ (that is, the Maruts, who are regularly called nс╣Ы╠Б-). See vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гamaс╣Зas- in 7c.

P─Бda c presents the crucial moment in the RV svayaс╣Гvara, the brideтАЩs mounting the chariot of the groom (see Jamison 2001, Fs. Parpola). On a possible preterital tr. of ─Б╠БтАж g─Бt see comm. on the next vs. _________ 06
The decisive moment of mounting is repeated immediately in this verse, in the causative ─Б╠Бsth─Бpayanta. The -anta form can be simply an -anta replacement of act. -an of the usual type (Jamison 1979), but it might also be semantically justified: тАЬThey cause(d) her to mount (their own chariot).тАЭ As Hoffmann points out, ─Б╠Бsth─Бpayanta need not be read as impf. ─Б╠Б asth─Бpayanta with the Pp., but can be an injunctive ─Б╠Бsth─Бpayanta. The published translation has preterital тАЬcaused тАж to mount.,тАЭ and I still think that is correct, though a general present could provide an easy transition to the here-and-now of the ritual found in cd.

My reason for preferring the preterital reading has to do with my view of the structure of the middle section of the hymn: vss. 3-6ab treat the mythological relationship between Rodas─л and the Maruts, while 6cd-7 bring Rodas─л and the Maruts into the ritual present. I see vid├бtheс╣гu in 6b as the pivot: on the one hand it echoes vidathy─Б╠Аin 3d and provides ring-compositional closure to the mythological section of the hymn; on the other hand it looks forward to the ritual present 6cd.

Since the chariot mounting of 6a is part of the mythological past, a preterital (or timeless) tr. fits it better. (It might also be better to tr. the injunc. ─Б╠БтАж g─Бt in 5c in the same preterital fashion.) In the published translation I take ┼Ыubh├й with the preceding p─Бda: тАЬmount for beauty,тАЭ since ┼Ы├║bh- is very commonly used in Marut hymns to refer to their journey (cf., e.g.,

Griffith

When chose immortal Rodasi to follow–she with loose tresses and heroic spirit–
She climbed her servant’s chariot, she like Surya with cloud-like motion and refulgent aspect.

Als es der Asurischen gefiel, sie zu begleiten, der mannhaftgesinnten Rodasi mit aufgel├╢sten Z├╢pfen, so bestieg sie wie Surya den Wagen des Verehrers, von funkelndem Aussehen wie das Nahen der Wetterwolke.

Grassmann

Wenn sie nun will die himmlische begleiten, gel├╢sten Haars die m├дnnerholde Jungfrau, Dann komme wie die Sonne sie ergl├дnzend, wie aus der Wolke zu des Treuen Wagen.

English translation:

тАЬThe youthful (Maruts) have plural ced the young (lightning) in (their) brilliant (car), commingling (with them), and vigorous (in yielding rain) on sacrifices (being solemnized); when, Maruts, your worshipper, presenting oblations, pouring out the Soma, and offering adoration, chants the sacred song.тАЭ

рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдВ рдпрдГ рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛ рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддрд┐рд╢рдпрдГ рд╡рдХреНрдореНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрдГ рдЕрдмрд╛рдзреНрдпреЛрд╜рдореЛрдШрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрдВ рдкреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрдорд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдЪреНрдорд┐ рд╡рд░реНрдгрдпрд╛рдорд┐ ред рдХрдердореЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдИрдореН рдПрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреА рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рд╡реГрд╖рдордгрд╛рдГ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрдордирд╕реНрдХрд╛ рдЕрд╣рдВрдпреБрдГ рдЕрд╣рдВрдХрд╛рд░рд╡рддреА ред рдЬрдЧрджреБрдкрдХрд╛рд░рдХрд░реНрддреНрд░реА рди рдХрджрд╛рдЪрд┐рджрд╕реНрддреАрддреНрдпрд╣рдВрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рд╛ рдЪрд┐рддреН ред рдЪрд┐рджрд┐рддрд┐ рдкреВрдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН ред рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдорд╡рд┐рдирд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛ рдИрджреГрд╢реА рджреЗрд╡реА рд╕реБрднрд╛рдЧрд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирднрд╛рдЧреНрдпреЛрдкреЗрддрд╛рдГ рдЬрдиреАрдГ рдЬрдирдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛: рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддреАрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╣рддреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ ред рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреМ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рди рдЙрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреЗрд╡рдВ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рддрдВ рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрддреМрдореАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI celebrate that greatness of the Maruts, which is true, and worthy of celebration, inasmuch as their high-minded,haughty, and ever-enduring (bride), supports a flourishing progeny.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

High-minded, haughty: The epithets, vс╣Ыс╣гamaс╣З─Б, ahaс╣Гyuс╕е, sthir─Б are feminine nine; the reference is to Rodas─л, the wife of the Maruts, who, by contributing to the rain, assists in the sustenance of mankind

Jamison Brereton

I proclaim what of theirs is worthy of proclamation, that the greatness of the Maruts is truly present,
when in company with them, her mind set on the bulls, she, self-reliant and firm, brings with her the well-portioned Wives (of the Gods).

Jamison Brereton Notes

For my tr. of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гamaс╣Зas- see disc. of nс╣Ыm├бс╣Зas- in 5b.

Geldner suggests that the greatness of the Maruts (p─Бda b) is demonstrated by the fact that Rodas─л happily brings along their other lovers without jealousy. This seems like an interpretational male fantasy to me (though I realize that our poet is also male and therefore likely prone to the same fantasy). I have a much soberer and less entertaining interpr. based in ritual. In the plural, j├бn─л- is regularly used of the wives of the gods, esp. in regard to their attendance at certain rituals. They are ordinarily brought by Tvaс╣гс╣нar, but here Rodas─л, one of their own, as it were, seems to stand in as their chaperon and cicerone. In the с╣Ъtugraha offerings (the тАЬsequential cupsтАЭ), in which a fixed order of gods receives oblations, the offering to the Maruts is followed immediately by one to Tvaс╣гс╣нar along with the wives of the gods; see I.15.2-3, II.36.2-3 (II.36.3d tv├бс╣гс╣нar dev├йbhir j├бnibhiс╕е sum├бdgaс╣Зaс╕е). Thus, given the temporal proximity of the oblations made to them at this ritual, one might expect to find both the Maruts and the wives of the gods together on the ritual ground.

I do not understand the force of cid in d, and in fact I think itтАЩs been automatically imported from the passages containing sthir─Б╠Бcid where the adj. is a neut. pl. and the point is that our hero (whoever it happens to be) has destroyed various items тАЬeven though they are firm/hardтАЭ (I.127.4, IV.7.10, VIII.20.1). In other words, I do not think it has a function here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMitra and Varuс╣Зa, and Aryaman, defend (this) sacrifice from (all that is) reprehensible, and destroy (all that are) unworthy. They cause the yet unfallen and showering (rains) to descend, when, Maruts, the water-yielding (season) gives increase to this (world).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

When the water-yielding season: v─Бvс╣Ыdha im maruto d─Бtiv─Бraс╕е: the last term may refer to the yajam─Бna; i.e. when, Maruts, the worshipper, or he by whom the offering is presented, promotes this your increase

Jamison Brereton

Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (and Aryaman) protect from the unspeakable (fault); Aryaman makes the unlaudable (men) atone.
And the unstirrable fixed things stir, (when) your wish-granting (flock) has grown strong, o Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Because the verb in p─Бda a, p─Б╠Бnti, is plural, not dual, at least one additional subject is needed in addition to du. mitr─Б╠Бv├бruс╣З─Б. The obvious one to supply is their partner Aryaman, who appears in the next p─Бda.

In d Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou, and Witzel Got┼Н identify d─Б╠Бtiv─Бraс╕е тАШwish-grantingтАЩ as the mortal sacrificer, although, as they all acknowledge, the other two occurrences of this stem modify the Maruts (III.51.9, V.58.2) and therefore the Maruts should be presumed to be the default referent here as well. I see no reason to contravene this expectation. In V.58.2 the adjective is singular, modifying gaс╣З├б- тАШflockтАЩ, a regular cover term for the Maruts, and I have supplied gaс╣З├б- here as well. I also consider d to be an unsignaled dependent clause тАЬ(when),тАЭ indicating the circumstances under which the unstirrable things stir (c), viz. when the Maruts get strong. The verb would have accent in any case because it is initial in its p─Бda. I do not, however, understand the ─лm in d, which has no referent, since v─Бvс╣Ыdh├й is intransitive (pace Grassmann). Taking the Maruts as the subj.

of v─Бvс╣Ыdh├й also fits nicely with 9, which treats the тАЬswelling strengthтАЭ (┼Ы├бvas-) of the Maruts.

Griffith

Mitra and Varuna they guard from censure: Aryaman too, discovers worthless sinners Firm things are overthrown that ne’er were shaken: he prospers, Maruts, who gives choice oblations.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNone of us, Maruts, have attained, either nearly or remotely, the limit of your strength; those (Maruts), increasing in energy and vigour, overwhelm their enemies like an ocean.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For they have not reached the limit of your swelling strength, o Maruts, nearby to us nor even in the distance.
These (Maruts), swollen with bold swelling strength, have boldly
hemmed in hatred like a flood.

Griffith

None of us, Maruts, near or at a distance, hath ever reached the limit of your vigour.
They in courageous might still waxing boldly have compassed round their foemen like an ocean.

Geldner

Denn niemals hat man das Ende eurer Macht, ihr Marut, weder nah noch fern von uns erreicht. Durch ihre k├╝hne Kraft ├╝berlegen, wehren sie k├╝hnlich der Anfeindungen wie einer Wasserflut.

Grassmann

Denn nie erreichen, nahe nicht, noch ferne, o Maruts, andre eurer St├дrke Ende; Mit k├╝hner Kraft umgebt ihr nun gekr├дftigt gleich wie ein Meer mit keckem Muth die Feinde.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрджреНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рджрд┐рдиреЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрддрдорд╛ рднрд╡реЗрдо ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрддрдорд╛ рд╡рдпрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдорд╣рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реЛрдЪреЗрдорд╣рд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдВ рд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛ рднреВрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдо ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдкрд┐ рджрд┐рдиреЗ рд╕рдорд░реНрдпреЗ ред рд╕рд╣ рдорд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕ рд╕рдорд░реНрдпреЛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГ рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН ред рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реЛрдЪреЗрдорд╣рд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╡рдпрдВ рдкреБрд░рд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирддреАрддреЗрд╜рдкрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдорд╣рд┐ рдорд╣рджреНрдмрд▓рдВ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрд░реНрдердВ рд╡реЛрдЪреЗрдорд╣рд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рджреНрдпреВрдиреН рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рд╛рди рдЕрдиреБ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрддреАрддреЗ рдЖрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдирд┐ рдЪ рджрд┐рд╡рд╕реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╡реЛрдЪреЗрдорд╣рд┐ ред рддрддреН рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдЛрднреБрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ ред рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред тАШрдЛрднреБрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдГ рдЙрдХреНрд╖рд╛’ (рдирд┐. рей. рей. резреж) рдЗрддрд┐ рддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рдорд╣рд╛рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдирд░рд╛рдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЕрдиреБ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдЕрдиреБ рднрд╡рддреБ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓рдорднрд┐рдорддрдкреНрд░рджреЛ рд╡рд╛ рднрд╡рддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us, who are beloved of Indra, glorify him today; let us glorify him tomorrow, at the sacred rite; let us glorify him for our great (good), in future days as of old, so that с╣Ъbhukс╣гin may ever be favourable to us amongst men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might we today, might we tomorrow call ourselves dearest to Indra in the competition,
(as) we (did) before, and let this be a great thing for us through the
days: let the R╠еbhu-ruling (flock) consisting of (these) superior men
[=Maruts] stay by us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

с╣Ыbhukс╣г─Б╠Бin d may refer to the Maruts collectively, as IтАЩve taken it, or to Indra, already mentioned in ab. Renou suggests both possibilities, though he goes for Indra in his tr. (as do Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н). It is true that singular с╣Ыbhukс╣г─Б╠Бс╕е generally refers to Indra, while it is plural с╣Ыbhukс╣г├бnaс╕е that qualifies the Maruts (VIII.7.9, 12, etc.). As in 8d IтАЩm taking interpreting the singular as collective referring to the Marut flock. If the referent is taken as Indra, the tr. should be altered to тАЬthe с╣Ъbhu-master of the superior men,тАЭ which seems a bit awkward.

Griffith

May we this day be dearest friends of Indra, and let us call on him in fight to-morrow.
So were we erst. New might attend us daily! So be with us! Rbhuksan of the Heroes!

Geldner

Wir wollen heut, wir morgen in dem Streite des Indra liebste Freunde hei├Яen. Wir waren es fr├╝her. Und Gro├Яes soll uns Tag f├╝r Tag werden: Das m├╢ge das Oberhaupt der M├дnner uns gestatten.

Grassmann

Wir seien heut des Indra auserlesne, wir wollen morgen ihn zum Kampfe rufen, Von ihm geliebt zuvor und fort und fort auch; drum steh uns bei der Ribhuherr der M├дnner.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis praise, Maruts, is for you, this hymn is for you, (the work) of a venerable author, capable of conferring delight (by his laudations); may the praise reach you for (the good of your) person ns, so that we may thence obtain food, strength, and long life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here is a praise for you, Maruts, here a hymn from M─Бnd─Бrya, the respectful bard.
With refreshment he would beg propitiation for himself. тАУ May we
know refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See comm. ad I.166.15.

Griffith

May this your laud, may this your song, O Maruts, sung by the poet, Mana’s
son, Mandarya,
Bring offspring for ourselves with. food to feed us. May we find strengthening food in full abundance.

Grassmann

Euch, Maruts, gilt dies Lied des Manasohnes, das Lob des Dichters von dem Stamm Mand─Бra’s, Mit Labung kommt herbei zu eigner St├дrkung gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╕рдмрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЖрдкреНрдд рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдФрд░ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдмрд▓ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рд╕рдореНрдкрд╛рджрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рд╕реЗ рдЬреАрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее резрез реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдХреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрдд рд╕реЗ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рд╕рдордЭрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рд╕рд░рд╕рдард╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдкрд╛рдБрдЪрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддреЛ рдПрд╖ рд╡рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореЛ рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╛рд░реЛрд░рд┐рдпрдЩреНрдЧреАрд░рд╕реНрддрд┐ред рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рд╜рд╜рдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╖реНрдЯ рд╡рдпрд╛рдВ рддрдиреНрд╡реЗ рддрд╛рдорд┐рд╖рдВ рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдВ рд╡реГрдЬрдирдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрд╖рдГ) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╕реНрддреЛрдордГ) рд╕реНрддрд╡рдирдореН (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ (рдЗрдпрдореН) (рдЧреАрдГ) рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдгреА (рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрдкреНрд░рджреЛрддреНрддрдорд╕реНрдп (рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рдХрд╛рд░реЛрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдГ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдЗрд╖рд╛) рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ (рдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╖реНрдЯ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рддрдиреНрд╡реЗ) рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдп (рд╡рдпрд╛рдореН) рд╡рдпрдореН (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рдо (рдЗрд╖рдореН) (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) рдмрд▓рдореН (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрдореН рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╢реНрд▓рд╛рдШреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордмрд▓рд╛рдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдореМ рд╕рдЮреНрдЪрд┐рдиреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рее резрез реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрди рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрдирдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдмреЛрдзреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╖рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдиреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд, рдЖрдкреНрдд рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрдирд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд. рд╢рд░реАрд░ рд╡ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдпрд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рдмрд▓ рд╡рд╛рдврд╡рд┐рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдареА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрди рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдиреЗ рдЬрдЧрддрд╛рдд. рее резрез рее
